The cleaning mode in the base is handy but as other reviewers have noted, you can accomplish the same level of cleaning by running the head and foils under warm water. I do like the fact that the base has an internal fan and a drying mode that can be used without having to go through the entire cleaning cycle. Overall a very good razor.

  26. I'm 68 so I have used a LOT of shavers over a LOT of years! This is definitely the best I have ever used. I have always really preferred a wet shave with a safety razor because that is the closest shave. However, with very sensitive skin, I can only shave with a blade about once a week so I have used electric shavers extensively over the years. This Panasonic shaver is definitely THE BEST I'VE EVER USED! It truly gives a shave as close as a safety razor. And it is very easy on my skin - I don't even need to use alcohol / shave lotion after shaving with this one - and can use it every day (though I seldom do anymore). It works well with a 3 day beard, too - but I find I need to start with a very light touch and then go back over - and still the same clean, close shave.<br /><br /> I especially like the cleaning unit - it leaves the razor as clean as brand new. Now, I always shave dry - and after shaving pop the head against the sink to remove the loose whisker and skin and a quick brushing of the top of the shaver itself. So, when I put it in the cleaner, all that loose debris is already removed - I think that probably makes the cleaning cartridge last a little longer and stay cleaner. The real effect of the cleaner, after all, is to remove all the skin oil that can build up in the shaving head so it is truly sparkling clean. I find the cleaning cartridge lasts me 2 months. At about a month along, a little more water needs to be added to the tank as a good bit apparently evaporates while the cleaning is being done; if the water level runs too low the cleaner will indicate a replacement cartridge is needed. NEVER replace all the water - the water in the tank has the cleaning 'soap' in it. The cartridge has a filter to take out larger particles (e.g. whiskers) and much of the dead skin, oils, etc. which is washed out of the shaver head and the water cycles through this on the way back to the tank. When replacing the cartridge, empty the water tank and then refill it and give it a good shake to pick up any sediment in the bottom of the tank and empty that out so you'll start the new cartridge with a very clean tank of water. Be sure to put your fingers over the two holes in the tank or you'll have water everywhere!

  57. I bought this Panasonic (ES-LT71-S Arc3) razor a couple of years ago to replace my old Braun Syncro razor after learning that Braun had decided to economize their blade designs and manufacture them in China with the result that it wasn't possible to buy quality replacement blades for the Braun anymore. The Panasonic has been a nice razor and I haven't had any problems with it. It shaves just as well as the Braun did or any electric razor I have had. The cleaning station for the razor is not as effective and integral as the cleaning station was for the Braun. In fact, if I recall correctly, the manual for the Panasonic indicates it's not that essential to use the cleaning station and you can just wash the razor off when you are in the shower or whatever. The cleaning station does keep the foil and blades clean and fresh for the next time you shave, but lower on the razor's head gunk will gradually build up. The cleaning station itself also gradually gunks itself up and has to be cleaned every 6-12 months or so. The razor's waterproof feature is really nice and it is super easy to clean it off in the sink or shower, and a wet shave does feel nice and gets closer than a dry shave. But I usually shave dry. The Panasonic's battery life and ability to keep a charge is much better than the Braun's ever was. I haven't had any more problems with it pulling my beard if I go a few days without shaving than I have with any other electric razor. It's just a problem inherent to electric razors, in my experience. All in all this is a good quality product and I wouldn't hesitate to purchase it again.

The LT71 has only one such intermediate foil. I could however not detect any difference in closeness of shave, both are excellent and better than my old and the new Braun I tried. It is identical to the LT71 except it has no cleaning device. This device seems unnecessary, though. Cleaning under running water, and if necessary adding some soap, cleans the shaver to a like new condition.<br />The LT41 and LT71 seem to replace the [[ASIN:B001DNE3KQ Panasonic ES8103S Men's 3-Blade (Arc 3) Wet/Dry Rechargeable Electric Shaver with Nanotech Blades, Silver]] and [[ASIN:B000VKZMHK Panasonic ES8109S Men's 3-Blade (Arc 3) Wet/Dry Nanotech Rechargeable Electric Shaver with Vortex Cleaning System, Silver]].   346. Since there are so many reviews, I will focus on what I have not seen in other reviews and what I believe is the biggest design flaw in this product. The shaver is fine, and I have no problems with it. But if you're buying this unit, it's probably because you want the cleaning system, too, so be aware...<br /><br />This purchase replaced an older Panasonic model where the razor was held in place by snapping into a piece that came over the top of the razor and cleaner. I never had any problems with this setup, but Panasonic decided to make it simpler, by having a system where you just drop the razor in the cleaner, the razor leans *slightly* back, and cleaning starts at the press the button. The problem with this is that without something holding the razor in place, it easily slips.<br /><br />As the razor cleans itself, the cleaner activates the razors blades to shake off debris. Unfortunately, while doing this, the razor very subtly moves itself out of place from the 3 metal contacts that it uses to charge and connect to the cleaner. As it cleans, it goes through cycles of turning the blades on and off as it pumps water through, but since it loses contact, it will stop vibrating before it is supposed to and the razor doesn't get fully cleaned -- or charged!<br /><br />I've &#34;fixed&#34; this by putting small items under the front of the cleaning system to make the razor lean back far enough so it can't shake itself out of place, but this is a ridiculous fix. I've used it for six months and there is no &#34;breaking in&#34; period after which this works better.

I've heard (read) others talk about the shave not being as close with an electric shaver, but that hasn't been so in my case. The shave I get with this razor is every bit as close. I really like being able to grab this razor to shave while soaking in the tub or showering.<br /><br />I almost didn't buy this razer because of the price. There are many cheaper electric razors. While I'm still not thrilled about the price, I'm happy with my choice for more reasons than just performance. Besides being able to take it in the shower, the shaver's cleaning cycle is awesome. I remember my dad's electric razor and its funky high school gym shower smell. This Pansonic Arc 3 stays fresh smelling and new feeling. The soap cartridge lasts a couple of months and is easily replaced; the old one slides out and the new one pops right back in. 3 seconds, tops.<br /><br />Another reason I was able to justify this purchase is the availability of replacement parts, like the soap cartridges. It is recommended that the outer foil and inner blade be replaced at least every year to maintain the cutting edge. Panasonic has been making shavers of this design for years and, as far as I can tell, the foil and blades remain the same even when model numbers change. That's great news because I feel secure that the inner workings of the shaver or cleaning system won't become obsolete. I'm keeping this baby for a good decade.<br /><br />Besides price, the only other issue I've had with this shaver is that I've had to twice replace the foil. Both times were my fault. The foil was damaged when I dropped the shaver once in the shower and once in the sink. I can't blame the shaver because the handle is made well enough to be able to hold on to it even when wet. I'm a klutz, so be warned if you are one too.e shaver or cleaning system won't become obsolete. The special setting for high speed vibration for cleaning doesn't seem to do anything special-- in fact, less hair or water come off in that mode than if you simply turn the unit on without the top attached! I haven't ventured to use the wet cleaning system, since I don't feel any special need for it and am somewhat dubious about cleanup and storage once the cleanser is installed.<br /><br />Bottom line: for me this has been a great razor, rendering closer shaves than any of the previous units I've used 40 years of daily (or even more frequent!) electric razor use since the 1970's.   444. I went from a Norelco floating head rotary razor to this Panasonic foil razor. They are different, but I'm not sure I would call one better than the other. I would say that the Panasonic probably gives a slightly closer shave and gets some places like the upper lip a little better than the Norelco. I also personally find it slightly less irritating to my neck which for me is extra sensitive and it trims sideburns better since it has a straght blade. However the flip side is I find it doesn't contain all the stubble dust in the shaver head. If I shave after I am dressed it leaves dust on the front of my shirt that has to be brushed off. It also does not do as well as the Norelco shaving my chin area.<br /><br />I think the differences in performance mostly come down to the differences in the way the two types function. The Norelco cuts in circular patterns and you use a circular pattern when you are shaving with it, so it catches stubble from multiple directions, with and against the grain. In addition the floating heads conform to irregular surfaces like the chin better than the flat surface of a foil head. Where the Panasonic excels is on flatter surfaces like the neck and cheek and it seems to cover more surface area in a single pass. However be warned that you may have to turn the Panasonic around and shave the opposite or opposing direction to shave against the grain to get the closest shave with it.<br /><br />It all comes down to personal choice. Both of mine still work so I can alternate back and forth for various reasons, I like them both. The alternative is shaving with a blade. I still prefer using an electric shaver over shaving with a blade for daily use. All I can say is try a foil or rotary shaver and make your own choice. As long as you don't go too cheap on either type, I doubt you can go wrong. My only other caution would be that if you have been shaving with a blade there is usually an adjustment period going to an electric shaver. Your skin has tobe conditioned to it, this usually takes a couple weeks. See the manufacturer's recommendations on this. If you give up on it in less time, it is probably not the razors fault.<br /><br />If you're trying to make a choice, I hope this helps.
